  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a0b211b9-97f1-4ab4-a9c4-850aa14553bd'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="review_2696694705" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2696694705" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2696694705?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=comics-graphic-novels">comics-graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2696694705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8245581679147559066"><i>“There's this idea that if you're not straight, you have to tell all your family and friends immediately, like you owe it to them. But you don't. You don't have to do anything until you're ready.”</i><br/><br/>I adore everything that Alice Oseman writes and Heartstopper is no exception. Obviously. It's so wholesome and heart-warming, so cute and lovely. It's a feel-good read, for sucky days and happy days alike. Something to make a sunny day brighter and something to hide under the covers with when you can't </span>
  <span id="freeText8245581679147559066" style="display:none"><i>“There's this idea that if you're not straight, you have to tell all your family and friends immediately, like you owe it to them. But you don't. You don't have to do anything until you're ready.”</i><br /><br />I adore everything that Alice Oseman writes and Heartstopper is no exception. Obviously. It's so wholesome and heart-warming, so cute and lovely. It's a feel-good read, for sucky days and happy days alike. Something to make a sunny day brighter and something to hide under the covers with when you can't stand anything else. Heartstopper is a lifesaver.<br /><br />I am so proud of Alice. I was really excited when I first heard of a book called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20618110.Solitaire" title="Solitaire by Alice Oseman" rel="nofollow noopener">Solitaire</a> that was going to be released soon, by an author barely older than myself. And I've devoured everything Alice published since then. I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25322449.Radio_Silence" title="Radio Silence by Alice Oseman" rel="nofollow noopener">Radio Silence</a> even better than her debut, and I fell completely in love with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34325090.I_Was_Born_for_This" title="I Was Born for This by Alice Oseman" rel="nofollow noopener">I Was Born for This</a>. Then, of course, there are Nick &amp; Charlie. When I saw that <i>Hearstopper: Volume Three</i> had snatched a place on the British Children's bestselling list, I felt so proud. Not only is this Alice's 6th book, it's also a) a graphic novel about b) queer teens and c) the third book in a series. The chances of a book like this to land on the Sunday Times best-selling list isn't very high. But with an ever-growing, super devoted fandom and Alice's loveliness and talent, anything is possible. I hope that the studio that bought the film rights to this series will take this as a sign and hurry up with finding a screenwriter, director, cast, etc. and just give us what we deserve.<br /><br />The volume itself was really cute. Overall it's fantastic that we get so much queer rep, even if some narrow-minded people might call it unrealistic. It makes me happy to see ace, trans, gay, bi, lesbian, and more characters living and loving and flourishing. It makes me happy to see a healthy discussion about sexuality, relationships and mental health. I love that these books are on bookshelves in stores and libraries and teenagers have access to them, can learn from them, see themselves in them, find hope in them.<br /><br />I do feel that, while it's all cute and funny, some moments are somewhat exaggerated. I mean, that much drama about a single hickey? Then again, maybe I'm forgetting what it was like to be 16 (and while I personally would have been o v e r d r a m a t i c should I have had a hickey, I doubt anyone else would have given a single...well).<br /><br />I so look forward to Volume 4, but my most anticipated release is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42115981.Loveless" title="Loveless by Alice Oseman" rel="nofollow noopener">Loveless</a>. I'm honestly so excited.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8245581679147559066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10987860544613052818" style="display:none">You know that moment when your entire soul melts into a book because it is warm and comfortable and safe, but also relatable and vulnerable and sometimes sad?? Me. And Heartstopper Vol 3. 🥺I am such a pile of emotions right now. This book is a warm hug and wholly uplifting, but it also touches on a lot of the harder parts of being a teen and queer and figuring it all out. Like how things can be okay <i>now</i>, but it doesn't erase bad things in the past. Mental illness is an insidious beast and it sometimes never leaves. And coming out isn't just a one time thing. AND YOUR ANXIETY OVER ALL OF IT IS VALID, NO MATTER WHAT. <br /><br />I felt so emotional in this one, and I love seeing these two grow. But also the side-characters are so dimensional and interesting too! (Also ALED!!!) (And someone was reading Radio Silence!!! That was meta!!) Also can we talk about the teachers?! I loved them.<br /><br />I love these novels so so much. I just. Have written such a sloppy review but they mean the world.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3214084593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10587247987579339719">Volume 3 of Alice Oseman's amazing <b>
  <i>Heartstopper</i>
</b> series hit me square in the feels, just like the last two books!<br/><br/>Nick and Charlie and their friends return in this, the third volume of Oseman’s amazing graphic novel series about young love, struggling with your identity, and finding the courage to be who you are and be with whom you choose.<br/><br/>Nick has just come out to his mother and he and Charlie take tentative steps toward becoming boyfriends. But both are nervous about how everyone—their frien</span>
  <span id="freeText10587247987579339719" style="display:none">Volume 3 of Alice Oseman's amazing <b>
  <i>Heartstopper</i>
</b> series hit me square in the feels, just like the last two books!<br /><br />Nick and Charlie and their friends return in this, the third volume of Oseman’s amazing graphic novel series about young love, struggling with your identity, and finding the courage to be who you are and be with whom you choose.<br /><br />Nick has just come out to his mother and he and Charlie take tentative steps toward becoming boyfriends. But both are nervous about how everyone—their friends and other classmates—will react to their being together, especially Charlie, who remembers being bullied horribly when he came out last year.<br /><br />On a school trip to Paris, Nick and Charlie become more comfortable with their relationship and each other—and being open about it with their friends. And Nick and Charlie aren’t the only ones feeling romantically inspired in the City of Love!!<br /><br />This series is so wonderfully drawn and is so beautifully heartfelt. Volume 3 touches lightly on mental illness and eating disorders and I imagine Volume 4 will address those issues more. (I hope I don't have to wait a long time for Volume 4. I don't know what I'll do!)<br /><br />Even in moments of seriousness this book is so full of joy and love and wonder. I’ll trot out my broken record and say I wish books like these existed when I was younger, but I’m so glad LGBTQIA kids have them now.<br /><br />This series doesn’t stop my heart, it makes it grow 10 sizes larger!! Kudos to Oseman for another beautiful, meaningful book.<br /><br />Check out my list of the best books I read in 2019 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2019.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2019.html</a>. <br /><br />Check out my list of the best books of the decade at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/my-favorite-books-of-decade.html" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/my-favorite-books-of-decade.html</a>.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>.<br /><br />Follow me on Instagram at <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener"> https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10587247987579339719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText4628631246530530134" style="display:none">Adorable &amp; real as I knew it would be!<br /><br />Nick and Charlie are officially dating, and a school trip to Paris with all their friends sounds perfect!<br /><br />But with Nick still not completely out yet, and a few homophobic assholes around things were never gonna run smoothly. <br /><br />I love all the different characters in here, I love the difficult issues Alice Osman tackles including homophobia, self harm and eating disorders. I’m sad that I have to wait until 2021 for the next instalment. But I can’t wait for more Nick and Charlie. <br /><br />Also I mentioned in my review of volume 1 that I didn’t see Charlie as much of a Slytherin - which is what Alice Osman classed him as in the bio, but he was definitely more Slytherin in here, in the best way! <br /><br />4 stars ⭐️ </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10227156183239459538">My heart feels so warm after reading this. Nick and Charlie and their group of friends must be protected at all cost, I swear! I appreciate Oseman's way of bringing out of the surface things most of us are afraid or hesitant to talk about. Communication and acceptance for me are the main things about here. There was drama but at the same time not overly done? Just the proper amount to spice things up and to give the characters the chance to talk about their issues. Love this!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText18417435719396306609" style="display:none">✨Alice Oseman, you're saving the world and ME!<br /><br />What's new?<br />This volume is as super cute as the last volume but this one is more intense and there's more stories than just Charlie's and Nick's. <br />This particular volume describes about a Paris trip. <br /><br />The series has become more intense in the sense that both the main characters are becoming more mature, taking things in their stride with much understanding and they come out much braver. <br /><br />This series is becoming more and more interesting because of the fact that it showcases very important issues related to the generation today regarding mental health issues where one of the main characters is dealing with eating disorders and depression with suicidal tendencies. It also shows how a person can deal with homophobia and how important it's to have the support of the people who we trust no matter how few they are.<br /><br />I seriously cannot wait for the next volume as it seems it will become more intense and I am sure it will mainly deal with eating disorders and the characters becoming more open and honest with each other. <br /><br />Damn my damn heart. It's all so soft and vibrating at the moment.</span>

<div id="review_3040672081" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3040672081" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1170391-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590218363p2/1170391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3040672081?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3040672081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18260069038959132484">There's something so comforting and safe and lovely about these comics. Alice Osemsn has managed to create an environment that feels like a wholesome community of good friends. It's a place where you can discuss anything and you'll be accepted no matter what.<br/><br/>I wish these were around when I was younger. In this edition we see Nick and Charlie visiting Paris on a school trip with some friends. After just coming out to his mum, Nick is now faced with the decision of when to come out to his friends,</span>
  <span id="freeText18260069038959132484" style="display:none">There's something so comforting and safe and lovely about these comics. Alice Osemsn has managed to create an environment that feels like a wholesome community of good friends. It's a place where you can discuss anything and you'll be accepted no matter what.<br /><br />I wish these were around when I was younger. In this edition we see Nick and Charlie visiting Paris on a school trip with some friends. After just coming out to his mum, Nick is now faced with the decision of when to come out to his friends, as well as juggling a very new relationship. Charlie in addition is still struggling with his own mental health demons, and I thought the issues covered were handled very sensitively and with a degree of compassion and understanding with important conversations about recovery. We also get more time with side characters Tao, Elle and Co who all have their own issues too. They all feel well developed and complicated and real. <br /><br />I will say that this volume didn't quite match the previous two for me in terms of tension and chemistry. Now Nick and Charlie are together they've lost a little of that angst I loved so much. But that's only a little issue. I still love them both. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18260069038959132484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3169953044" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3169953044" />
    <a title="Meags" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8542123-meags"><img alt="Meags" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524277146p2/8542123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3169953044?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meags" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meags" href="/user/show/8542123-meags">Meags</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=webcomics-and-graphic-novels">webcomics-and-graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=friends-to-lovers">friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=disability-illness-mentalhealth">disability-illness-mentalhealth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=bi-ofy-gfy">bi-ofy-gfy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=teachers-and-librarians">teachers-and-librarians</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3169953044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9248001498637604708"><b>4 Stars</b><br/><br/>This third volume of Charlie and Nick’s teenage love story is steadily becoming a bit more thoughtful, but no less romantic or addictive. In this installment, Oseman introduces themes surrounding mental health, that will surely become a bigger deal as the series (first and foremost <a href='https://heartstoppercomic.tumblr.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>a successful webcomic</a>) progresses.<br/><br/>Here, we follow newly established boyfriends Charlie and Nick as they head off to Paris on a school trip during summer. Nick is still struggling with how to come out as bisexua</span>
  <span id="freeText9248001498637604708" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars</b><br /><br />This third volume of Charlie and Nick’s teenage love story is steadily becoming a bit more thoughtful, but no less romantic or addictive. In this installment, Oseman introduces themes surrounding mental health, that will surely become a bigger deal as the series (first and foremost <a href="https://heartstoppercomic.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">a successful webcomic</a>) progresses.<br /><br />Here, we follow newly established boyfriends Charlie and Nick as they head off to Paris on a school trip during summer. Nick is still struggling with how to come out as bisexual, but having successfully come out to his supportive mother, he’s feeling a bit more at ease with himself, even encouraging Charlie to share their relationship status with his close friends (who are also on the trip). <br /><br />Being away from home and dealing with the stresses of travel, on top of their coming-out-as-a-couple news, results in Charlie becoming quite stressed and anxious, to the point that he has Nick worrying about his health and questioning whether Charlie’s issues may be way more serious than he’s letting on.<br /><br />I love that the series is getting more complex and serious, both in terms of character development and plot growth, exploring all sorts of prevalent mental health issues that teenagers the world over experience in their day-to-day lives. It’s particularly good to see such themes represented in a positive and proactive way that readers can engage and relate to.<br /><br />Knowing what I already know about Charlie at this time in his life, having just read Oseman’s debut novel Solitaire – which is set a year or so after these Heartstopper events – makes my heart ache all the more for Charlie and Nick and the serious health struggles Charlie is about to endure. At the end of the day, though, I adore these two together and I love how supportive and loving they are with one another, even in these early days of their relationship when things were so scary and new.<br /><br />I can’t wait to see what happens next in the Heartstopper series. Even though I sort of know where it’s going, based on my knowledge of the connected future-set novels/novellas, I can't wait to sink my teeth into more. &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="9248001498637604708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3200290353?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/32710668-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3200290353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2555342077219129355">Will Nick and Charlie ever stop being the cutest couple there is? I don't think so. I just love them so much, they feel very realistic and you can clearly see how much they deeply care for each other. This volume here follows the Paris trip that their school organizes and so we see them having a week full of exploring French museums and having fun. If you aren't caught up yet, I strongly suggest you give this comic book a chance!</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GtBuK33huknnKQFDBO074VKTZ7nmelbCoGYwB0Qyacpb70emiRvMCFkcbbeN6Bbf7QgGuE6APyrczSTClUrUvg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kRH/nw4V0u6jWo4oUkyqOoV3kqMXYjf3sDpaJj8Ap+3QLtYS+u+krx1v4tzbSYcEOuzzor+YXh/MkU7j7ngamQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5631140239151403640">Alice Oseman is an author/illustrator and was born in 1994 in Kent, England. She has written four YA contemporary novels about teenage disasters: SOLITAIRE, RADIO SILENCE, I WAS BORN FOR THIS, and LOVELESS. She is also the creator of LGBTQ+ YA romance webcomic HEARTSTOPPER, which is now published in physical form by Hachette Children's Books.<br/><br/>Alice’s first novel SOLITAIRE was published when she was</span>
  <span id="freeText5631140239151403640" style="display:none">Alice Oseman is an author/illustrator and was born in 1994 in Kent, England. She has written four YA contemporary novels about teenage disasters: SOLITAIRE, RADIO SILENCE, I WAS BORN FOR THIS, and LOVELESS. She is also the creator of LGBTQ+ YA romance webcomic HEARTSTOPPER, which is now published in physical form by Hachette Children's Books.<br /><br />Alice’s first novel SOLITAIRE was published when she was nineteen. Her YA novels have been nominated for the YA Book Prize, the Inky Awards, and the Goodreads Choice Award, and HEARTSTOPPER has been optioned for TV. She can usually be found staring aimlessly at computer screens, questioning the meaninglessness of existence, or doing anything and everything to avoid getting an office job.</span>
